	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">South India</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

		<div id="contentSub"></div>

<li><a href="/wiki/Urdu_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu Language">Urdu</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>South India</b> is the area including the five southern <a href="/wiki/States_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="States of India">Indian states</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telangana" title="Telangana">Telangana</a>, as well as the three <a href="/wiki/Union_territories_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Union territories of India">union territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Andaman and Nicobar islands">Andaman and Nicobar islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">Lakshadweep</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puducherry" title="Puducherry">Puducherry</a>, occupying 19% of India's area (635,780&#160;km<sup>2</sup> or 245,480&#160;sq&#160;mi). Covering the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsular</a> <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan Plateau</a>, South India is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> in the east, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> in the south. The geography of the region is diverse with two mountain ranges–the <a href="/wiki/Western_Ghats" title="Western Ghats">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ghats" title="Eastern Ghats">Eastern Ghats</a>, bordering the <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> heartland. <a href="/wiki/Godavari_River" title="Godavari River">Godavari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaveri_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaveri River">Kaveri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungabhadra_River" title="Tungabhadra River">Tungabhadra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Periyar_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Periyar River">Periyar</a> , <a href="/wiki/Vaigai_River" title="Vaigai River">Vaigai</a> , <a href="/wiki/Palar_River" title="Palar River">Palar River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponnaiyar" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponnaiyar">Ponnaiyar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thamiraparani" class="mw-redirect" title="Thamiraparani">Thamiraparani</a> rivers are important non-<a href="/wiki/Perennial_stream" title="Perennial stream">perennial</a> sources of water. <a href="/wiki/Bengaluru" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengaluru">Bengaluru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_Telangana" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, Telangana">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore" title="Coimbatore">Coimbatore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trivandrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Trivandrum">Trivandrum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam" title="Visakhapatnam">Visakhapatnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vijayawada" title="Vijayawada">Vijayawada</a>-<a href="/wiki/Guntur" title="Guntur">Guntur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajamahendravaram" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajamahendravaram">Rajamahendravaram</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kakinada" title="Kakinada">Kakinada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Tamil_Nadu" title="Salem, Tamil Nadu">Salem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vellore" title="Vellore">Vellore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiruchirapalli" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiruchirapalli">Tiruchirapalli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madurai" title="Madurai">Madurai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mysuru" class="mw-redirect" title="Mysuru">Mysuru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mangalore" title="Mangalore">Mangalore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Kozhikode</a> are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_million-plus_urban_agglomerations_in_India" title="List of million-plus urban agglomerations in India">largest urban areas</a>.
</p><p>The majority of the people in South India speak one of the four major <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian languages</a>: <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a>,  and <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>. During its <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_India" title="History of South India">history</a>, a number of dynastic kingdoms ruled over parts of South India whose invasions across <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">southeastern</a> Asia impacted the history and culture in those regions. Major dynasties that were established in South India include the <a href="/wiki/Chera_dynasty" title="Chera dynasty">Cheras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Cholas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandyan_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Pandyan dynasty">Pandyas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallava_dynasty" title="Pallava dynasty">Pallavas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satavahana_dynasty" title="Satavahana dynasty">Satavahanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">Chalukyas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta_dynasty" title="Rashtrakuta dynasty">Rashtrakutas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara</a>. Some Western European countries established ports in the region by military coercion in the 18th and 19th centuries.
</p><p>After experiencing fluctuations in the decades immediately after <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence</a>, the economies of South Indian states have registered higher than national average growth over the past three decades.  While South Indian states have improved in some <a href="/wiki/Socio-economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economics">socio-economic</a> metrics, poverty continues to affect the region much like the rest of the country, although it has considerably decreased over the years. <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a> in the southern states is high and the economy has undergone growth at a faster rate than most northern states. <a href="/wiki/Literacy_in_India" title="Literacy in India">Literacy rates</a> in the southern states are higher than the national average with approximately 80% of the population capable of reading and writing. The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> in South India is 1.9, the lowest of all regions in India.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dravida_nadu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dravida_nadu.jpg/220px-Dravida_nadu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dravida_nadu.jpg/330px-Dravida_nadu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dravida_nadu.jpg/440px-Dravida_nadu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dravida_nadu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South India</div></div></div>
<p>South India, also known as Peninsular India, has been known by several other names. The term "Deccan", referring to the area covered by the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Plateau" title="Deccan Plateau">Deccan Plateau</a> that covers most of peninsular India excluding the coastal areas, is an anglicised form of the <a href="/wiki/Prakrit_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Prakrit language">Prakrit</a> word <i>dakkhin</i> derived from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> word <i>dakshina</i> meaning south.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <i>Carnatic</i>, derived from <i>"Karnād"</i> or <i>"Karunād"</i> meaning <i>high country</i>, has also been associated with South India.<sup id="cite_ref-hobsons_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hobsons-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_India" title="History of South India">History of South India</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_era">Ancient era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rajendra_map_new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Rajendra_map_new.svg/200px-Rajendra_map_new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Rajendra_map_new.svg/300px-Rajendra_map_new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Rajendra_map_new.svg/400px-Rajendra_map_new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="465" data-file-height="333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rajendra_map_new.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chola_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Chola Empire">Chola Empire</a> during Rajendra Chola I, c. 1030</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carbon_dating" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon dating">Carbon dating</a> on ash mounds associated with <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> cultures in South India date back to 8000&#160;BCE. Odisha was the first state and one of early adopter to South Indian culture. For the benefit South India, Odisha donated all of its wealth. Artefacts such as ground stone axes, and minor copper objects have been found in the region. Towards the beginning of 1000&#160;BCE, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">iron technology</a> spread through the region; however, there does not appear to be a fully developed <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> preceding the Iron Age in South India.<sup id="cite_ref-prehistory_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prehistory-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The region was in the middle of a trade route that extended from <a href="/wiki/Muziris" title="Muziris">Muziris</a> to <a href="/wiki/Arikamedu" title="Arikamedu">Arikamedu</a> linking the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Trade with <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Syria" title="Demographics of Syria">Syrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> began from the <a href="/wiki/Sangam_period" title="Sangam period">Sangam period</a> (c. 3rd century BC to c. 4th century AD).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The region was part of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> connecting the Asian continent in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">East</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several tamil dynasties such as the <a href="/wiki/Chera_dynasty" title="Chera dynasty">Cheras</a> of <a href="/wiki/Karur" title="Karur">Karuvur</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pandyas" class="mw-redirect" title="Pandyas">Pandyas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Madurai" title="Madurai">Madurai</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cholas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cholas">Cholas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Thanjavur" title="Thanjavur">Thanjavur</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Satavahanas" class="mw-redirect" title="Satavahanas">Satavahanas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Amaravathi_village,_Guntur_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaravathi village, Guntur district">Amaravati</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pallavas" class="mw-redirect" title="Pallavas">Pallavas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kanchi" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanchi">Kanchi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kadambas" class="mw-redirect" title="Kadambas">Kadambas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Banavasi" title="Banavasi">Banavasi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Ganga_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Ganga Dynasty">Western Gangas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kolar" title="Kolar">Kolar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta" class="mw-redirect" title="Rashtrakuta">Rashtrakutas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manyakheta" class="mw-redirect" title="Manyakheta">Manyakheta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">Chalukyas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Badami" title="Badami">Badami</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hoysalas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoysalas">Hoysalas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Belur,_Karnataka" title="Belur, Karnataka">Belur</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kakatiya_dynasty" title="Kakatiya dynasty">Kakatiyas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Warangal" title="Warangal">Orugallu</a> ruled over the region from 6th century B.C. to 14th century A.D. The <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara Empire</a>, founded in 14th century A.D. was the last Indian dynasty that ruled over the region. After repeated invasions from the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Delhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Delhi">Sultanate of Delhi</a> and the fall of Vijayanagara empire in 1646, the region was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Sultanates" class="mw-redirect" title="Deccan Sultanates">Deccan Sultanates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palaiyakkarar" class="mw-redirect" title="Palaiyakkarar">polygars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nayak_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nayak dynasty">Nayak</a> governors of Vijayanagara empire who declared independence.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Europeans arrived in the 15th century and by the middle of the 18th century, the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British</a> were involved in a protracted struggle for military control over the South India. After the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Tipu_Sultan" title="Tipu Sultan">Tipu Sultan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Mysore_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Mysore War">Fourth Anglo-Mysore War</a> in 1799 and the end of the <a href="/wiki/Vellore_Mutiny" class="mw-redirect" title="Vellore Mutiny">Vellore Mutiny</a> in 1806, the British consolidated their power over much of present-day South India with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Pondicherry district">French Pondichéry</a>. The <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> took control of the region from the British East India Company in 1857.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> During the British colonial rule, the region was divided into the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Presidency" title="Madras Presidency">Madras Presidency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State" title="Hyderabad State">Hyderabad State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">Mysore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thiruvithamcoore" class="mw-redirect" title="Thiruvithamcoore">Travancore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kochi" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Kochi">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vizianagaram" title="Vizianagaram">Vizianagaram</a> and a number of other minor <a href="/wiki/Princely_state" title="Princely state">princely states</a>. The region played a major role in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a>; of the 72 delegates who participated in the first session of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> at Bombay in December 1885, 22 hailed from South India.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence">Post-independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Indian_territories.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/South_Indian_territories.svg/200px-South_Indian_territories.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/South_Indian_territories.svg/300px-South_Indian_territories.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/South_Indian_territories.svg/400px-South_Indian_territories.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="672" data-file-height="746" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Indian_territories.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of South India (1953–1956) before the States Reorganisation Act of 1956</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence of India">independence of India</a> in 1947, the region was organised into four states: <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_State_(1948%E2%80%9356)" title="Hyderabad State (1948–56)">Hyderabad State</a> and Travancore-Cochin.<sup id="cite_ref-Article_1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Article_1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="States Reorganisation Act">States Reorganisation Act</a> of 1956 reorganised the states on linguistic lines resulting in the creation of the new states of Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka, Kerala and Tamil Nadu.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a result of this Act, Madras State retained its name and <a href="/wiki/Kanyakumari_district" title="Kanyakumari district">Kanyakumari district</a> was added to it from the state of Travancore-Cochin.<sup id="cite_ref-1956act_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956act-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The state was subsequently renamed Tamil Nadu in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-1956act_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956act-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Andhra Pradesh was created through the merger of <a href="/wiki/Andhra_State" title="Andhra State">Andhra State</a> with the Telugu-speaking districts of the Hyderabad State in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-1956act_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956act-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Kerala emerged from the merger of <a href="/wiki/Malabar_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Malabar district">Malabar district</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kasaragod_taluk" title="Kasaragod taluk">Kasaragod taluk</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Canara" title="South Canara">South Canara</a> districts of the <a href="/wiki/Madras_State" title="Madras State">Madras State</a> with Travancore-Cochin.<sup id="cite_ref-1956act_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956act-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State" title="Mysore State">Mysore State</a> was re-organised with the addition of districts of <a href="/wiki/Bellary_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellary district">Bellary</a> and South Canara (excluding Kasaragod <i>taluk</i><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_1"><a href="#endnote_1">Note 1</a></sup>) and the <a href="/wiki/Kollegal" title="Kollegal">Kollegal taluk</a> of <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore_district" title="Coimbatore district">Coimbatore district</a> from the Madras State, the districts of <a href="/wiki/Belgaum_district" title="Belgaum district">Belgaum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bijapur_district,_Karnataka" title="Bijapur district, Karnataka">Bijapur</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Canara" class="mw-redirect" title="North Canara">North Canara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dharwad_district" title="Dharwad district">Dharwad</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_State" title="Bombay State">Bombay State</a>, the Kannada-majority districts of <a href="/wiki/Bidar" title="Bidar">Bidar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raichur" title="Raichur">Raichur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulbarga" title="Gulbarga">Gulbarga</a> from the Hyderabad State and the province of <a href="/wiki/Coorg" class="mw-redirect" title="Coorg">Coorg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1956act_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1956act-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Mysore State was renamed as Karnataka in 1973. The <a href="/wiki/Union_territory" title="Union territory">Union territory</a> of Puducherry was created in 1954 comprising the previous <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French</a> enclaves of Pondichérry, <a href="/wiki/Karaikal" title="Karaikal">Karaikal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yanam,_French_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Yanam, French India">Yanam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_India" title="Mahé, India">Mahé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Laccadive_Islands" title="Laccadive Islands">Laccadive Islands</a>, which were divided between South Canara and Malabar districts of Madras State, were united and organised into the union territory of Lakshadweep. Telangana was created on 2 June 2014 by bifurcating Andhra Pradesh and it comprises ten districts of the erstwhile state of Andhra Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span> <i>Taluk</i> is a smaller administrative division than a district
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_South_India" title="Geography of South India">Geography of South India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_India_satellite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/South_India_satellite.jpg/200px-South_India_satellite.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/South_India_satellite.jpg/300px-South_India_satellite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/South_India_satellite.jpg/400px-South_India_satellite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_India_satellite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of South India</div></div></div>
<p>South India is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> in the shape of an inverted triangle bound by the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> on the west, by the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> on the east and <a href="/wiki/Vindhya" class="mw-redirect" title="Vindhya">Vindhya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Satpura" class="mw-redirect" title="Satpura">Satpura</a> ranges on the north.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Narmada_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Narmada river">Narmada river</a> flows westwards in the depression between the Vindhya and Satpura ranges which define the northern spur of the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Deccan plateau">Deccan plateau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Western_Ghats" title="Western Ghats">Western Ghats</a> run parallel along the western coast and the narrow strip of land between the Western Ghats and the Arabian Sea forms the <a href="/wiki/Konkan" title="Konkan">Konkan</a> region. The Western Ghats continue south until <a href="/wiki/Kanyakumari" title="Kanyakumari">Kanyakumari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ghats" title="Eastern Ghats">Eastern Ghats</a> run parallel along the eastern coast and the strip of land between the Eastern Ghats and the Bay of Bengal forms the <a href="/wiki/Coromandel_Coast" title="Coromandel Coast">Coromandel</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Both the ranges meet at the <a href="/wiki/Nilgiris_(mountains)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nilgiris (mountains)">Nilgiri</a> mountains. The Nilgiris run in a crescent approximately along the borders of Tamil Nadu with northern Kerala and Karnataka, encompassing the <a href="/wiki/Palakkad_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Palakkad District">Palakkad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayanad" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayanad">Wayanad</a> hills and the <a href="/wiki/Sathyamangalam" title="Sathyamangalam">Sathyamangalam</a> ranges, extending on to the relatively low-lying hills of the Eastern Ghats on the western portion of the Tamil Nadu–Andhra Pradesh border forming the <a href="/wiki/Tirumala_-_Tirupati" class="mw-redirect" title="Tirumala - Tirupati">Tirupati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annamalai_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Annamalai Hills">Annamalai</a> hills.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The low-lying <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> islands of Lakshadweep are situated off the southwestern coast of India. The <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar" class="mw-redirect" title="Andaman and Nicobar">Andaman and Nicobar</a> islands lie far off the eastern coast of India. The <a href="/wiki/Palk_Strait" title="Palk Strait">Palk Strait</a> and the chain of low sandbars and islands known as <a href="/wiki/Rama%27s_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Rama&#39;s Bridge">Rama's Bridge</a> separate the region from <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, which lies off the southeastern coast.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The southernmost tip of mainland India is at <a href="/wiki/Kanyakumari_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanyakumari (town)">Kanyakumari</a> where the Indian Ocean meets the Bay of Bengal and the Arabian Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Deccan plateau is the elevated region bound by the mountain ranges.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The plateau rises to 100 metres (330&#160;ft) in the north and to more than 1 kilometre (0.62&#160;mi) in the south, forming a raised triangle within the downward-pointing triangle of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>'s coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> It also slopes gently from West to East resulting in major rivers arising in the Western Ghats and flowing east into the Bay of Bengal.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The volcanic <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> beds of the Deccan were laid down in the massive <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Traps" title="Deccan Traps">Deccan Traps</a> eruption, which occurred towards the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> period between 67 and 66 million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Layer after layer was formed by the volcanic activity that lasted 30,000&#160;years<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and when the volcanoes became extinct, they left a region of highlands with typically vast stretches of flat areas on top like a table.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The plateau is watered by east flowing rivers <a href="/wiki/Godavari_River" title="Godavari River">Godavari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaveri" title="Kaveri">Kaveri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaigai" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaigai">Vaigai</a>. The major tributaries include <a href="/wiki/Pennar" class="mw-redirect" title="Pennar">Pennar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungabhadra" class="mw-redirect" title="Tungabhadra">Tungabhadra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhavani_River" title="Bhavani River">Bhavani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thamirabarani_River" title="Thamirabarani River">Thamirabarani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg/200px-India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="226" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg/300px-India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg/400px-India_climatic_zone_map_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1639" data-file-height="1852" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Climatic zones</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg/200px-India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="226" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg/300px-India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg/400px-India_southwest_summer_monsoon_onset_map_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1639" data-file-height="1852" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Southwest monsoon currents</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The region has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> and depends on monsoons for rainfall. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, it has a non-<a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> climate with minimum mean temperatures of 18&#160;°C (64&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The most humid is the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> characterised by moderate to high year-round temperatures and seasonal heavy rainfall above 2,000&#160;mm (79&#160;in) per year. The tropical climate is experienced in a strip of south-western lowlands abutting the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast" title="Malabar Coast">Malabar Coast</a>, the Western Ghats and the islands of Lakshadweep and Andaman and Nicobar are also subject to this climate.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical wet and dry climate</a>, drier than areas with a tropical monsoon climate, prevails over most of the inland peninsular region except for a semi-arid <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> east of the Western Ghats. Winter and early summer are long and dry periods with temperatures averaging above 18&#160;°C (64&#160;°F), summer is exceedingly hot with temperatures in low-lying areas exceeding 50&#160;°C (122&#160;°F), and the rainy season lasts from June to September with annual rainfall averaging between 750 and 1,500&#160;mm (30 and 59&#160;in) across the region. Once the dry northeast monsoon begins in September, most precipitation in India falls in Tamil Nadu, leaving other states comparatively dry.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> predominates the land east of the Western Ghats and the <a href="/wiki/Cardamom_Hills" title="Cardamom Hills">Cardamom Hills</a>. The region, which includes Karnataka, inland Tamil Nadu and western Andhra Pradesh, gets between 400 and 750 millimetres (15.7 and 29.5&#160;in) of rainfall annually with hot summers and dry winters with temperatures around 20–24&#160;°C (68–75&#160;°F). The months between March and May are hot and dry with mean monthly temperatures hover around 32&#160;°C (90&#160;°F), with 320 millimetres (13&#160;in) precipitation, and without artificial irrigation, this region is not suitable for agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">southwest monsoon</a> from June to September accounts for most of the rainfall in the region. The Arabian Sea branch of the southwest monsoon hits the Western Ghats along the coastal state of Kerala and moves northwards along the <a href="/wiki/Konkan_coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Konkan coast">Konkan coast</a> with precipitation on coastal areas, west of the Western Ghats. The lofty Western Ghats prevent the winds from reaching the Deccan Plateau; hence, the leeward region (the region deprived of winds) receives very little rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The Bay of Bengal branch of the southwest monsoon heads toward northeast India, picking up moisture from the Bay of Bengal. The <a href="/wiki/Coramandel_coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Coramandel coast">Coramandel coast</a> does not receive much rainfall from the southwest monsoon due to the shape of the land. <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> and southeast <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a> receive rains from the northeast monsoon.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The northeast monsoon takes place from November to early March when the surface <a href="/wiki/High-pressure_system" class="mw-redirect" title="High-pressure system">high-pressure system</a> is strongest.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Indian_Ocean_tropical_cyclone" title="North Indian Ocean tropical cyclone">North Indian Ocean tropical cyclones</a> occur throughout the year in the Bay of Bengal and the Arabian Sea, bringing devastating winds and heavy rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elephas_maximus_(Bandipur).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg/200px-Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg/300px-Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg/400px-Elephas_maximus_%28Bandipur%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2598" data-file-height="1732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elephas_maximus_(Bandipur).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South India has the largest elephant population.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Karnataka" title="Wildlife of Karnataka">Wildlife of Karnataka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Tamil_Nadu" title="Wildlife of Tamil Nadu">Wildlife of Tamil Nadu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kerala" title="Wildlife of Kerala">Wildlife of Kerala</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_South_India" title="List of birds of South India">List of birds of South India</a></div>
<p>There is a wide diversity of plants and animals in South India, resulting from its varied climates and geography. <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Ghats_moist_deciduous_forests" title="South Western Ghats moist deciduous forests">Deciduous forests</a> are found along the Western Ghats while <a href="/wiki/South_Deccan_Plateau_dry_deciduous_forests" title="South Deccan Plateau dry deciduous forests">tropical dry forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deccan_thorn_scrub_forests" title="Deccan thorn scrub forests">scrub lands</a> are common in the interior Deccan plateau. The southern Western Ghats have rainforests located at high altitudes called the <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Ghats_montane_rain_forests" title="South Western Ghats montane rain forests">South Western Ghats montane rain forests</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_Coast_moist_forests" title="Malabar Coast moist forests">Malabar Coast moist forests</a> are found on the coastal plains.<sup id="cite_ref-netgeo_terres_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-netgeo_terres-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Western Ghats is one of the eight hottest <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspots</a> in the world and a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Important ecological regions of South India are the <a href="/wiki/Nilgiri_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Nilgiri Biosphere Reserve">Nilgiri Biosphere Reserve</a>, located at the conjunction of the borders of Karnataka, Kerala and Tamil Nadu in the <a href="/wiki/Nilgiri_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Nilgiri Hills">Nilgiri Hills</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anamalai_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Anamalai Hills">Anamalai Hills</a> in the Western Ghats. Bird sanctuaries including <a href="/wiki/Vedanthangal_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Vedanthangal Bird Sanctuary">Vedanthangal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranganathittu_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Ranganathittu Bird Sanctuary">Ranganathittu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumarakom_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Kumarakom Bird Sanctuary">Kumarakom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neelapattu_Sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Neelapattu Sanctuary">Neelapattu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulicat_Lake" title="Pulicat Lake">Pulicat</a> are home to numerous migratory and local birds.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Lakshadweep has been declared a bird sanctuary by the <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_Institute_of_India" title="Wildlife Institute of India">Wildlife Institute of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wii_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wii-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Other protected ecological sites include the <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove forests</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pichavaram" title="Pichavaram">Pichavaram</a> in Tamil Nadu, the <a href="/wiki/Backwater_(river)" title="Backwater (river)">backwaters</a> of Pulicat lake in Tamil Nadu and <a href="/wiki/Vembanad_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Vembanad Lake">Vembanad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashtamudi_Lake" title="Ashtamudi Lake">Ashtamudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paravur_Kayal" class="mw-redirect" title="Paravur Kayal">Paravur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayamkulam" title="Kayamkulam">Kayamkulam</a> lakes in Kerala. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mannar_Biosphere_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf of Mannar Biosphere Reserve">Gulf of Mannar Biosphere Reserve</a> covers an area of 10,500&#160;km<sup>2</sup> of ocean, islands and the adjoining coastline including <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">salt marshes</a> and mangroves. It is home to <a href="/wiki/Endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Endangered">endangered</a> aquatic species including <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dugong" title="Dugong">dugongs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holothuroidea" class="mw-redirect" title="Holothuroidea">sea cucumbers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The region is home to one of the largest populations of endangered <a href="/wiki/Indian_elephant" title="Indian elephant">Indian elephant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tiger</a> in India. Elephant populations are found in eight fragmented sites in South India; in northern Karnataka, along the Western Ghats, in <a href="/wiki/Bhadra_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Bhadra Wildlife Sanctuary">Bhadra</a>–<a href="/wiki/Malnad" class="mw-redirect" title="Malnad">Malnad</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Brahmagiri_(hill)" class="mw-redirect" title="Brahmagiri (hill)">Brahmagiri</a>–Nilgiris–Eastern Ghats, in <a href="/wiki/Nilambur" title="Nilambur">Nilambur</a>–<a href="/wiki/Silent_Valley_National_Park" title="Silent Valley National Park">Silent Valley</a>–Coimbatore, in <a href="/wiki/Anamalai" class="mw-redirect" title="Anamalai">Anamalai</a>–<a href="/wiki/Parambikulam" class="mw-redirect" title="Parambikulam">Parambikulam</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Periyar_National_Park" title="Periyar National Park">Periyar</a>–<a href="/wiki/Srivilliputhur" title="Srivilliputhur">Srivilliputhur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agasthyamalai" class="mw-redirect" title="Agasthyamalai">Agasthyamalai</a><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The region is home to one-third of the tiger population and more than half of the elephant population of India.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> There are 14 <a href="/wiki/Project_Tiger" title="Project Tiger">Project Tiger</a> <a href="/wiki/Tiger_reserves_of_India" title="Tiger reserves of India">reserves</a> and 11 <a href="/wiki/Project_Elephant" title="Project Elephant">Project Elephant</a> reserves in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Other threatened and endangered species found in the region include <a href="/wiki/Grizzled_giant_squirrel" title="Grizzled giant squirrel">grizzled giant squirrel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grey_slender_loris" class="mw-redirect" title="Grey slender loris">grey slender loris</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sloth_bear" title="Sloth bear">sloth bear</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nilgiri_tahr" title="Nilgiri tahr">Nilgiri tahr</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nilgiri_langur" title="Nilgiri langur">Nilgiri langur</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lion-tailed_macaque" title="Lion-tailed macaque">lion-tailed macaque</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_leopard" title="Indian leopard">Indian leopard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Dravidian people">Dravidian people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugus" class="mw-redirect" title="Telugus">Telugus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannadigas" class="mw-redirect" title="Kannadigas">Kannadigas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malayalis" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayalis">Malayalis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg/300px-SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg/450px-SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg/600px-SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SouthIndiaAgePyramid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population Pyramid in South India</div></div></div>
<p>As per the <a href="/wiki/2011_census_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 census of India">2011 census of India</a>, the estimated population of South India is 252 million, around one fifth of the total population of India. The region's <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) was less than the <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">population replacement level</a> of 2.1 for all states with Kerala and Tamil Nadu having the lowest TFRs in India at 1.7.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the proportion of the population of South India to India's total population has declined from 1981 to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The population density of the region is approximately 463. <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_Castes_and_Tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheduled Castes and Tribes">Scheduled Castes and Tribes</a> form 18% of the population of the region. Agriculture is the major employer in the region with 47.5% of the population is involved in agrarian activities.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> About 60% of the population lives in permanent housing structures.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> 67.8% of South India has access to tap water with wells and springs forming other major sources of water supply.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After experiencing fluctuations in the decades immediately after the independence of India, the economies of South Indian states have registered growth higher than the national average over the past three decades. While South Indian states have improved in some of the <a href="/wiki/Socio-economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economics">socio-economic</a> metrics,<sup id="cite_ref-outlook1_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outlook1-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ecoindicators_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecoindicators-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> poverty continues to affect the region as it does the rest of the country, although it has considerably decreased over the years. Basis the 2011 census, <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">HDI</a> in the southern states is high and the economy has grown at a faster rate than most northern states.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As per the 2011 census, the average <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> in South India is approximately 80%, considerably higher than the Indian national average of 74% with Kerala having the highest literacy rate of 93.91%.<sup id="cite_ref-lit_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lit-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> South India has the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> with Kerala and Tamil Nadu being the top two states.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The South Indian states rank amongst the top 10 in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Indian_states_ranked_by_economic_freedom&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Indian states ranked by economic freedom (page does not exist)">economic freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_by_life_expectancy_at_birth" title="List of Indian states by life expectancy at birth">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_states_ranking_by_drinking_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian states ranking by drinking water">access to drinking water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_states_ranking_by_families_owning_house" title="Indian states ranking by families owning house">house ownership</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_states_ranking_by_television_ownership" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian states ranking by television ownership">TV ownership</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_India" title="Poverty in India">Poverty</a> rate is at 19% while that in the other Indian states is at 38%. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> is <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>19,531</span> (US$280), which is more than double of the other Indian states (<span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>8,951</span> (US$130)).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Of the three demographic related targets of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a> set by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> expected to be achieved by 2015, Kerala and Tamil Nadu achieved the goals related to improvement of maternal health and of reducing infant mortality and child mortality by 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian languages</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DravidianTree.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/DravidianTree.png/300px-DravidianTree.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/DravidianTree.png/450px-DravidianTree.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/DravidianTree.png/600px-DravidianTree.png 2x" data-file-width="737" data-file-height="373" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DravidianTree.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dravidian language tree</div></div></div>
<p>The largest linguistic group in South India is the <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_family_of_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Dravidian family of languages">Dravidian family of languages</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">family</a> of approximately 73 languages<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The major languages spoken include <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannada" title="Kannada">Kannada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tulu_language" title="Tulu language">Tulu</a> is spoken by about 1.5&#160;million people in coastal Kerala and Karnataka and <a href="/wiki/Konkani_language" title="Konkani language">Konkani</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan</a> language, is spoken by half a million people in the Konkan coast, <a href="/wiki/Kodava_language" title="Kodava language">Kodava Takk</a> is spoken by more then half a million people in Kodagu, Mysore and Bangalore. English is also widely spoken in urban areas of South India.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> is spoken by around 12 million <a href="/wiki/Indian_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Muslims">Muslims</a> in southern India.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Tamil, Telugu, Kannada, Malayalam, Urdu and Konkani are listed amongst the 22 <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Official languages of India">official languages</a> of India as per the Official Languages Act (1963). Tamil was the first language to be granted <a href="/wiki/Classical_language_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical language in India">classical language</a> status by the Government of India in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Other major languages declared classical were Kannada (in 2008), Telugu (in 2008) and Malayalam (in 2013)<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">

<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a></td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:purple; width:8%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">8%</td>
</tr><tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:grey; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1%</td>
</tr>

</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the major religion with about 80% of the population adhering to it. About 11% of the population follow <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and 8% follow <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Evidence of <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_religion" title="Prehistoric religion">prehistoric religion</a> in South India comes from scattered <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> rock paintings depicting dances and rituals in <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Stone_Age" title="South Asian Stone Age">Stone Age</a> sites such as the <a href="/wiki/Kupgal_petroglyphs" title="Kupgal petroglyphs">Kupgal petroglyphs</a> of eastern Karnataka.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Hinduism, often regarded as the oldest religion in the world, traces its roots to prehistoric times in India.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The main spiritual traditions of South India include both <a href="/wiki/Shaivism" title="Shaivism">Shaivite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaishnavism" title="Vaishnavism">Vaishnavite</a> branches of Hinduism, although <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a> philosophies had been influential several centuries earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ayyavazhi" title="Ayyavazhi">Ayyavazhi</a> is spread significantly across the southern parts of South India.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Islam was introduced to South India in the early 7th century by <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> traders in Malabar Coast of Kerala and spread during the rule of Deccan Sultanates from 17th to 18th century and the Muslims in Kerala of Arab descent are called <a href="/wiki/Jonaka_Mappila" class="mw-redirect" title="Jonaka Mappila">Jonaka Mappila</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> According to tradition, Christianity was introduced to South India by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_the_Apostle" title="Thomas the Apostle">Thomas the Apostle</a>, who visited Muziris in Kerala in 52 CE and proselytized natives.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Kerala is also home to one of the oldest Jewish communities in the world who are supposed to have arrived in the Malabar coast during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Biblical_account_of_King_Solomon" class="mw-redirect" title="Biblical account of King Solomon">King Solomon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_South_India" title="Economy of South India">Economy of South India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Major_crop_areas_India.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Major_crop_areas_India.png/200px-Major_crop_areas_India.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Major_crop_areas_India.png/300px-Major_crop_areas_India.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Major_crop_areas_India.png/400px-Major_crop_areas_India.png 2x" data-file-width="1486" data-file-height="1734" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Major_crop_areas_India.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Major crop areas</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tidel_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Tidel_Park.jpg/200px-Tidel_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Tidel_Park.jpg/300px-Tidel_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Tidel_Park.jpg/400px-Tidel_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tidel_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The growth of information technology hubs in the region have spurred economic growth. Pictured is <a href="/wiki/Tidel_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidel Park">Tidel Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a></div></div></div>
<p>The economy of South India after the independence of the nation conformed to a <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> framework, with strict governmental control over <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private sector</a> participation, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign trade">foreign trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>. Through 1960 to 1990, the South Indian economies experienced mixed economic growth. In the 1960s, Kerala achieved above average economic growth while Andhra Pradesh's economy declined during this period. Kerala experienced an economic decline in the 1970s while the economies of Karnataka, Tamil Nadu and Andhra Pradesh consistently exceeded national average growth rates after 1970 due to <a href="/wiki/Economic_reforms_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic reforms in India">reform-oriented</a> economic policies compared to other Indian states.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017–18, the total <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross domestic product</a> of the region is <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>56 trillion</span> (US$810&#160;billion). <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_by_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Indian states by GDP">second</a> highest GDP and is the second most industrialised state in the country after <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2015, there are 109 operational <a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zone">Special Economic Zones</a> in South India, which is about 60% of the country's total.<sup id="cite_ref-Com_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Com-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over 48% of South India's population is engaged in agriculture, which is largely dependent on seasonal monsoons. Some of the main crops cultivated in South India include <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">paddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_millet" title="Pearl millet">pearl millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulses" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulses">pulses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile_pepper" class="mw-redirect" title="Chile pepper">chilli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finger_millet" class="mw-redirect" title="Finger millet">ragi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Areca" title="Areca">Areca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rubber" class="mw-redirect" title="Rubber">rubber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spices" class="mw-redirect" title="Spices">spices</a> are cultivated on the hilly regions. The staple food is rice; the delta regions of Godavari, <a href="/wiki/Krishna_River" title="Krishna River">Krishna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kaveri_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaveri River">Kaveri</a> are amongst the top rice producing areas in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Frequent droughts have left farmers debt-ridden, forcing them to sell their livestock and sometimes to commit suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The region accounts for 92% of the total <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_India" title="Coffee production in India">Coffee production in India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> South India is also a major producer of cotton, tea, rubber, <a href="/wiki/Turmeric" title="Turmeric">turmeric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a> and spices.<sup id="cite_ref-Com_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Com-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Other major agriculture related produce include <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bengaluru, Hyderabad, Chennai , Coimbatore and Thiruvananthapuram are amongst the major IT hubs of India and Bengaluru is also known as the <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> of India. The growth of information technology (IT) hubs in the region have spurred economic growth and attracted foreign investments and job seekers from other parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Software exports from South India grossed over <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>640 billion</span> (US$9.3&#160;billion) in fiscal 2005–06.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Chennai, known as the "<a href="/wiki/Detroit_of_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Detroit of Asia">Detroit of Asia</a>", accounts for about 35% of India's overall automotive components and automobile output.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The region supplies two-thirds of India's requirements of motors and pumps and is one of the largest exporters of jewellery, <a href="/wiki/Wet_grinder" title="Wet grinder">wet grinders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">auto components</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The other major industry is textiles<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> with the region being home to nearly 60% of the fibre textile mills in India.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_India" title="Tourism in India">Tourism</a> contributes significantly to the GDP of the region with three states – Tamil Nadu, Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka and Telangana – among the top 10 states for tourist arrivals and accounting for more than 50% of domestic tourist visits.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>South India consists of the five southern Indian states of Andhra Pradesh, Telangana, Karnataka, Kerala and Tamil Nadu as well as the union territories of Puducherry, Lakshadweep and Andaman and Nicobar.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Puducherry and the five states have an elected state government each, while the Lakshadweep and Andaman islands are <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">centrally</a> administered by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Each sub-region is further divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of India">districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Each state is headed by a Governor, who is a direct appointee of the President of India, while the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister">Chief Minister</a> is the elected head of the state government and represents the state's ruling party or <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States">States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ul><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^Note 1</a></b></span>  Andhra Pradesh was divided into two states, Telangana and a residual Andhra Pradesh on 2 June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_Of_India_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_Of_India-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-APGazetteMar4_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-APGazetteMar4-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad</a>, located entirely within the borders of Telangana, is to serve as joint capital for both states for a period of time not exceeding ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
