<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader" style="text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Legislative assemblies of states</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_St._George,_Chennai_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg/150px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg/225px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg/300px-Fort_St._George%2C_Chennai_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="2000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Fort_St._George,_India" title="Fort St. George, India">Fort St. George</a> (Tamil Nadu)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/150px-Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="84" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/225px-Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg/300px-Andhra_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="558" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Vidhan Bhavan (Telangana)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg/150px-Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg/225px-Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg/300px-Vidhana_Soudha_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2687" data-file-height="1000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Vidhan_Soudha" class="mw-redirect" title="Vidhan Soudha">Vidhan Soudha</a> (Karnataka)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Kerala_Legislative_Assembly,_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg/150px-Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="112" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg/225px-Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg/300px-Kerala_Legislative_Assembly%2C_Thiruvananthapuram.jpg 2x" data-file-width="996" data-file-height="746" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Niyamasabha_Mandiram" title="Niyamasabha Mandiram">Niyamasabha Mandiram</a> (Kerala)</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>South India elects 132 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament (India)">members</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a> accounting for roughly one-fourth of the total strength.<sup id="cite_ref-Lok_Sabha_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lok_Sabha-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The region has an allocation of 58 seats in <a href="/wiki/Rajya_Sabha" title="Rajya Sabha">Rajya Sabha</a> out of the total 245.<sup id="cite_ref-Rajya_Sabha_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajya_Sabha-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Each state is headed by a <a href="/wiki/Governor_(India)" title="Governor (India)">Governor</a>, who is a direct appointee of the President of India; the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister (India)">Chief Minister</a> is the elected head of the state government and represents the ruling party or coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Tamil Nadu, Kerala and Puducherry follow <a href="/wiki/Unicameral_legislature" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral legislature">unicameral legislature</a> while Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka and Telangana follow <a href="/wiki/Bicameral_legislature" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral legislature">bicameral legislature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vidhan_Sabha_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vidhan_Sabha-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Assembly">State legislatures</a> elect members for terms of five years.<sup id="cite_ref-Govt_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Govt-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> States with bicameral legislatures have an upper house (<a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Council">Legislative Council</a>) with members not more than one-third the size of the Assembly. Governors may suspend or dissolve assemblies and can administer when no party is able to form a government.<sup id="cite_ref-Govt_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Govt-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Each state is organised into a number of <a href="/wiki/District" title="District">districts</a>, which are further subdivided into revenue divisions and <i><a href="/wiki/Taluk" class="mw-redirect" title="Taluk">taluk</a></i>s (or <i>tehsil</i>s) for administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Govt_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Govt-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Local bodies govern respective cities, towns and villages with each electing a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipal chairman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panchayat" class="mw-redirect" title="Panchayat">panchayat chairman</a> respectively to head the same.<sup id="cite_ref-Govt_163-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Govt-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="sortable wikitable" style="font-size: 85%">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_in_South_India" title="Politics in South India">Politics in South India</a></div>
<p>Politics in South India is characterised by a mix of regional and national political parties. <a href="/wiki/Justice_Party_(India)" title="Justice Party (India)">Justice Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swaraj_Party" title="Swaraj Party">Swaraj Party</a> were the two major parties in the erstwhile Madras Presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopp_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopp-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The Justice Party eventually lost the <a href="/wiki/1937_Madras_Presidency_legislative_assembly_election" class="mw-redirect" title="1937 Madras Presidency legislative assembly election">1937 elections</a> to the Indian National Congress and <a href="/wiki/Chakravarti_Rajagopalachari" class="mw-redirect" title="Chakravarti Rajagopalachari">Chakravarti Rajagopalachari</a> became the Chief Minister of the Madras Presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopp_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopp-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> During the 1920s and 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Self-Respect_Movement" title="Self-Respect Movement">Self-Respect Movement</a> emerged in the Madras Presidency spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Theagaroya_Chetty" class="mw-redirect" title="Theagaroya Chetty">Theagaroya Chetty</a> and <a href="/wiki/E._V._Ramaswamy" class="mw-redirect" title="E. V. Ramaswamy">E. V. Ramaswamy</a> (commonly known as Periyar).<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In 1944 Periyar, who had started the Self-Respect Movement transformed the party into a social organisation, renaming the party <a href="/wiki/Dravidar_Kazhagam" title="Dravidar Kazhagam">Dravidar Kazhagam</a>, and withdrew from electoral politics. The initial aim was the secession of <a href="/wiki/Dravida_Nadu" title="Dravida Nadu">Dravida Nadu</a> from the rest of India on independence. After Independence, <a href="/wiki/C._N._Annadurai" title="C. N. Annadurai">C. N. Annadurai</a>, a follower of Periyar formed the <a href="/wiki/Dravida_Munnetra_Kazhagam" title="Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam">Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam</a> in 1948. The <a href="/wiki/Anti-Hindi_agitations_of_Tamil_Nadu" title="Anti-Hindi agitations of Tamil Nadu">Anti-Hindi agitations of Tamil Nadu</a>
led to the rise of Dravidian parties which formed its first government in 1967 in Tamil Nadu.  In 1972, a split in the DMK resulted in the formation of the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Anna_Dravida_Munnetra_Kazhagam" title="All India Anna Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam">All India Anna Dravida Munnetra Kazhagam</a> led by <a href="/wiki/M._G._Ramachandran" title="M. G. Ramachandran">M. G. Ramachandran</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_parties" title="Dravidian parties">Dravidian parties</a> continue to dominate Tamil Nadu electoral politics; the national parties usually aligned as junior partners to the major Dravidian parties, AIADMK and DMK.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Indian National Congress dominated the political scene in Tamil Nadu in 1950s and 1960s under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/K._Kamaraj" title="K. Kamaraj">K. Kamaraj</a>, who led the party after the death of <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> and ensured the selection of Prime Ministers <a href="/wiki/Lal_Bahadur_Shastri" title="Lal Bahadur Shastri">Lal Bahadur Shastri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Congress continues to be a major party in Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka and Kerala. The party ruled with minimal opposition for 30 years in Andhra Pradesh before the formation of <a href="/wiki/Telugu_Desam_Party" title="Telugu Desam Party">Telugu Desam Party</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nandamuri_Taraka_Rama_Rao" class="mw-redirect" title="Nandamuri Taraka Rama Rao">Nandamuri Taraka Rama Rao</a> in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Two prominent party systems in Kerala are the <a href="/wiki/United_Democratic_Front_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Democratic Front (India)">United Democratic Front</a>, led by the Indian National Congress and the <a href="/wiki/Left_Democratic_Front_(Kerala)" title="Left Democratic Front (Kerala)">Left Democratic Front</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_India_(Marxist)" title="Communist Party of India (Marxist)">Communist Party of India (Marxist)</a>. For the past fifty years, these two coalitions have been alternately in power and <a href="/wiki/E._M._S._Namboodiripad" title="E. M. S. Namboodiripad">E. M. S. Namboodiripad</a>, the first elected chief minister of Kerala in 1957 is credited as the leader of the first democratically elected communist government in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Janata_Dal" title="Janata Dal">Janata Dal</a> are significant parties in Karnataka.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>C. Rajagopalachari, the first Indian Governor General of India post independence, was from South India. The region has produced six Indian presidents namely <a href="/wiki/Sarvepalli_Radhakrishnan" title="Sarvepalli Radhakrishnan">Sarvepalli Radhakrishnan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/V._V._Giri" title="V. V. Giri">V. V. Giri</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neelam_Sanjiva_Reddy" title="Neelam Sanjiva Reddy">Neelam Sanjiva Reddy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/R._Venkataraman" class="mw-redirect" title="R. Venkataraman">R. Venkataraman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/K._R._Narayanan" title="K. R. Narayanan">K. R. Narayanan</a><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/APJ_Abdul_Kalam" class="mw-redirect" title="APJ Abdul Kalam">APJ Abdul Kalam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Prime Ministers</a> <a href="/wiki/P._V._Narasimha_Rao" title="P. V. Narasimha Rao">P. V. Narasimha Rao</a> and <a href="/wiki/H._D._Deve_Gowda" title="H. D. Deve Gowda">H. D. Deve Gowda</a> were from the region.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_heritage">Culture and heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture and heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_Indian_culture" title="South Indian culture">South Indian culture</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clothing">Clothing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Clothing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South Indian women traditionally wear a <i><a href="/wiki/Sari" title="Sari">sari</a></i>, a garment that consists of a drape varying from 5 yards (4.6&#160;m) to 9 yards (8.2&#160;m) in length and 2 feet (0.61&#160;m) to 4 feet (1.2&#160;m) in breadth that is typically wrapped around the waist, with one end draped over the shoulder, baring the midriff.<sup id="cite_ref-Saree_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saree-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Ancient Tamil poetry such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Silappadhikaram" class="mw-redirect" title="Silappadhikaram">Silappadhikaram</a></i> describes women in exquisite drapery or sari.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The sari is to be wrapped around the waist, with the loose end of the drape to be worn over the shoulder, baring the midriff as according to Indian philosophy, the navel is considered as the source of life and creativity.<sup id="cite_ref-Saree_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saree-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madisar" title="Madisar">Madisar</a> is a typical style worn by Brahmin ladies from Tamil Nadu.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Women wear colourful <a href="/wiki/Silk_saree" class="mw-redirect" title="Silk saree">silk sarees</a> on special occasions such as marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The men wear a <i><a href="/wiki/Dhoti" title="Dhoti">dhoti</a></i>, a 4.5 metres (15&#160;ft) long, white rectangular piece of non-stitched cloth often bordered in brightly coloured stripes. It is usually wrapped around the waist and the legs and knotted at the waist.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> A colourful <i><a href="/wiki/Lungi" title="Lungi">lungi</a></i> with typical <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a> patterns is the most common form of male attire in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-Cloth_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cloth-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> People in urban areas generally wear tailored clothing and western dress is popular in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Cloth_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cloth-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Western-style school uniforms are worn by both boys and girls in schools even in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Cloth_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cloth-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG/190px-Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG" decoding="async" width="190" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG/285px-Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG/380px-Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1721" data-file-height="1760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Veg_Full_Meals_in_Tamil_Nadu.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A traditional meal served on a banana leaf</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_Indian_cuisine" title="South Indian cuisine">South Indian cuisine</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">Rice</a> is the staple diet, while fish is an integral component of coastal South Indian meals.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">Coconut</a> and spices are used extensively in South Indian cuisine. The region has a rich cuisine involving both traditional non-vegetarian and vegetarian dishes comprising rice, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lentil" title="Lentil">lentils</a>. Its distinct aroma and flavour is achieved by the blending of <a href="/wiki/Flavouring" class="mw-redirect" title="Flavouring">flavourings</a> and spices including <a href="/wiki/Curry_tree" title="Curry tree">curry leaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustard_seed" title="Mustard seed">mustard seeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chili_powder" title="Chili powder">chili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">pepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clove" title="Clove">cloves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_cardamom" class="mw-redirect" title="Green cardamom">green cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>, coconut and <a href="/wiki/Rosewater" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosewater">rosewater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The traditional way of eating a meal involves being seated on the floor, having the food served on a <a href="/wiki/Banana_leaf" title="Banana leaf">banana leaf</a><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and using clean fingers of the right hand to take the food into the mouth.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> After the meal, the fingers are washed; the easily degradable banana leaf is discarded or becomes fodder for cattle.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Eating on banana leaves is a custom thousands of years old, imparts a unique flavor to the food and is considered healthy.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Idli" title="Idli">Idli</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dosa" title="Dosa">dosa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Uthappam" class="mw-redirect" title="Uthappam">uthappam</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Appam" title="Appam">appam</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pongal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pongal">pongal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Paniyaram" class="mw-redirect" title="Paniyaram">paniyaram</a></i> are popular dishes for breakfast.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Rice is served with <i><a href="/wiki/Sambar_(dish)" title="Sambar (dish)">sambar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rasam" title="Rasam">rasam</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Poriyal" title="Poriyal">poriyal</a></i> for lunch. <a href="/wiki/Telugu_cuisine" title="Telugu cuisine">Andhra cuisine</a> is characterised by <a href="/wiki/Pickling" title="Pickling">pickles</a> and spicy <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chettinad_cuisine" title="Chettinad cuisine">Chettinad cuisine</a> is famous for non-vegetarian items and <a href="/wiki/Hyderabadi_cuisine" title="Hyderabadi cuisine">Hyderabadi cuisine</a> is popular for its <i><a href="/wiki/Hyderabadi_biryani" title="Hyderabadi biryani">biryani</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:416px;max-width:416px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader" style="text-align:center;background-color:transparent">South Indian dance forms</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:SavithaPress1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SavithaPress1.jpg/100px-SavithaPress1.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SavithaPress1.jpg/150px-SavithaPress1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/SavithaPress1.jpg/200px-SavithaPress1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Bharatanatyam" title="Bharatanatyam">Bharatanatyam</a> (Tamil Nadu)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG/100px-Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG/150px-Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG/200px-Kathakali_IMG_0348_by_Joseph_Lazer.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5616" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Kathakali" title="Kathakali">Kathakali</a> (Kerala)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG/100px-A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG/150px-A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG/200px-A_Kuchipudi_Dancer_from_Andhra_Pradesh.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3600" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Kuchipudi" title="Kuchipudi">Kuchipudi</a> (Andhra Pradesh)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Demon_Yakshagana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Demon_Yakshagana.jpg/100px-Demon_Yakshagana.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Demon_Yakshagana.jpg/150px-Demon_Yakshagana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Demon_Yakshagana.jpg/200px-Demon_Yakshagana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="333" data-file-height="500" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Yakshagana" title="Yakshagana">Yakshagana</a> (Karnataka)</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The traditional music of South India is known as <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">Carnatic music</a>, which includes rhythmic and structured music by composers like <a href="/wiki/Purandara_Dasa" title="Purandara Dasa">Purandara Dasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanaka_Dasa" title="Kanaka Dasa">Kanaka Dasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyagayya" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyagayya">Tyagayya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annamacharya" title="Annamacharya">Annamacharya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhakta_Ramadasu" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhakta Ramadasu">Bhakta Ramadasu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muthuswami_Dikshitar" title="Muthuswami Dikshitar">Muthuswami Dikshitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shyama_Shastri" title="Shyama Shastri">Shyama Shastri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kshetrayya" title="Kshetrayya">Kshetrayya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mysore_Vasudevachar" title="Mysore Vasudevachar">Mysore Vasudevachar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swathi_Thirunal" class="mw-redirect" title="Swathi Thirunal">Swathi Thirunal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The main instrument that is used in South Indian Hindu temples is the <i><a href="/wiki/Nadaswaram" title="Nadaswaram">nadaswaram</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Reed_instrument" class="mw-redirect" title="Reed instrument">reed instrument</a> played along with <a href="/wiki/Thavil" title="Thavil">thavil</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Drum_instrument" class="mw-redirect" title="Drum instrument">drum instrument</a> to create an ensemble.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The motion picture industry has emerged as an important platform in South India over the years, portraying the cultural changes, trends, aspirations and developments experienced by its people. South India is home to several distinct dance forms such as <a href="/wiki/Bharata_Natyam" class="mw-redirect" title="Bharata Natyam">Bharatanatyam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kathakali" title="Kathakali">Kathakali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerala_Natanam" title="Kerala Natanam">Kerala Natanam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koodiyattam" title="Koodiyattam">Koodiyattam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuchipudi" title="Kuchipudi">Kuchipudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margamkali" title="Margamkali">Margamkali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohiniaattam" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohiniaattam">Mohiniaattam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oppana" title="Oppana">Oppana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottamthullal" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottamthullal">Ottamthullal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theyyam" title="Theyyam">Theyyam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vilasini_Natyam" title="Vilasini Natyam">Vilasini Natyam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yakshagana" title="Yakshagana">Yakshagana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The dance, clothing and sculptures of South India exemplify the beauty of the body and motherhood.<sup id="cite_ref-Saree_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saree-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Films in regional languages are prevalent; this includes <a href="/wiki/Kannada_cinema" title="Kannada cinema">Kannada cinema</a> (Karnataka), <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">Malayalam cinema</a> (Kerala), <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">Tamil cinema</a> (Tamil Nadu) and <a href="/wiki/Telugu_cinema" title="Telugu cinema">Telugu cinema</a> (Telangana and Andhra Pradesh). The first silent film in South India, <i><a href="/wiki/Keechaka_Vadham" title="Keechaka Vadham">Keechaka Vadham</a></i>, was made by <a href="/wiki/R._Nataraja_Mudaliar" title="R. Nataraja Mudaliar">R. Nataraja Mudaliar</a> in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-RANDOR_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RANDOR-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_South_India" title="Cinema of South India">South India</a>, the first Tamil talkie, <i><a href="/wiki/Kalidas_(film)" title="Kalidas (film)">Kalidas</a></i>, was released on 31 October 1931, barely seven months after India's first talking picture <i><a href="/wiki/Alam_Ara" title="Alam Ara">Alam Ara</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-velayutham2_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-velayutham2-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Mudaliar also established South India's first film studio in Madras.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Swamikannu_Vincent" class="mw-redirect" title="Swamikannu Vincent">Swamikannu Vincent</a> built the first cinema studio of South India in Coimbatore and introduced the concept of "tent cinema", the first of whose kind was established in Madras and was known as "Edison's Grand Cinemamegaphone".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Filmmakers <a href="/wiki/K_Balachandar" class="mw-redirect" title="K Balachandar">K Balachandar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balu_Mahendra" title="Balu Mahendra">Balu Mahendra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bharathiraaja" class="mw-redirect" title="Bharathiraaja">Bharathiraaja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a> in Tamil cinema, <a href="/wiki/Adoor_Gopalakrishnan" title="Adoor Gopalakrishnan">Adoor Gopalakrishnan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaji_N._Karun" title="Shaji N. Karun">Shaji N. Karun</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Abraham_(director)" title="John Abraham (director)">John Abraham</a> and <a href="/wiki/G._Aravindan" title="G. Aravindan">G. Aravindan</a> in Malayalam cinema, and <a href="/wiki/K._N._T._Sastry" title="K. N. T. Sastry">K. N. T. Sastry</a> and <a href="/wiki/B._Narsing_Rao" title="B. Narsing Rao">B. Narsing Rao</a> in Telugu cinema produced realistic parallel cinema throughout the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cinema has also <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema_and_Dravidian_politics" title="Tamil cinema and Dravidian politics">exerted its influence on politics</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> prominent film personalities like <a href="/wiki/C_N_Annadurai" class="mw-redirect" title="C N Annadurai">C N Annadurai</a>, <a href="/wiki/M_G_Ramachandran" class="mw-redirect" title="M G Ramachandran">M G Ramachandran</a>, <a href="/wiki/M_Karunanidhi" class="mw-redirect" title="M Karunanidhi">M Karunanidhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/N._T._Rama_Rao" title="N. T. Rama Rao">N. T. Rama Rao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jayalalithaa" title="Jayalalithaa">Jayalalithaa</a> have become Chief Ministers of South Indian states.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> As of 2014, South Indian film industries contribute to 53% of the total films produced in India.<sup id="cite_ref-film_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-film-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width:33em; text-align:center; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg/200px-Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg/300px-Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg/400px-Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madurai_meenakshi_temple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The large <i><a href="/wiki/Gopuram" title="Gopuram">gopuram</a></i> is a hallmark of <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_architecture" title="Dravidian architecture">Dravidian architecture</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>South India has an independent literary tradition dating back over 2500 years. The first known literature of South India is the poetic <a href="/wiki/Sangam_literature" title="Sangam literature"><i>Sangam</i> literature</a>, written in Tamil 2500 to 2100 years ago. The <a href="/wiki/Tamil_literature" title="Tamil literature">literature</a> was composed in three successive poetic assemblies known as <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Sangam" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamil Sangam">Tamil <i>Sangam</i>s</a> that were held in the ancient times on a now vanished <a href="/wiki/Kumari_Kandam" title="Kumari Kandam">continent</a> far to the south of India.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> This literature includes the oldest grammar treatise <i><a href="/wiki/Tholkappiyam" class="mw-redirect" title="Tholkappiyam">Tholkappiyam</a></i> and epics <i>Silappatikaram</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Manimekalai" title="Manimekalai">Manimekalai</a></i> written in Tamil.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> References to <a href="/wiki/Kannada_literature" title="Kannada literature">Kannada literature</a> appear from fourth century CE.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Telugu_literature" title="Telugu literature">Telugu literature</a> adopted a form of Prakrit which in course of development became the immediate ancestor of Telugu.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Distinct <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_literature" title="Malayalam literature">Malayalam literature</a> came later in the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South India has two distinct styles of rock architecture, the <i><a href="/wiki/Dravidian_architecture" title="Dravidian architecture">Dravidian</a></i> style of Tamil Nadu and the <i><a href="/wiki/Vesara" title="Vesara">Vesara</a></i> style of Karnataka.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The temples considered of porches or <i>mantapas</i> preceding the door leading to the sanctum, gate-pyramids or <i><a href="/wiki/Gopuram" title="Gopuram">gopurams</a></i>, which are the principal features in the quadrangular enclosures that surround the more notable temples and pillared halls used for many purposes and are the invariable accompaniments of these temples. Besides these, a South Indian temple typically has a tank called the <i>Kalyani</i> or <i>Pushkarni</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The <i>gopuram</i> is a monumental tower, usually ornate at the entrance of any temple in Southern India. This forms a prominent feature of <i><a href="/wiki/Koil" title="Koil">koil</a></i>s, <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple_architecture" title="Hindu temple architecture">Hindu temples</a> of the Dravidian style.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> They are topped by the <i>kalasam</i>, a spherical stone <a href="/wiki/Finial" title="Finial">finial</a>, and function as gateways through the walls that surround the temple complex.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The origins of the <i>gopuram</i> can be traced back to early structures of the Pallavas and by the twelfth century, under the Pandya rulers, these gateways became a dominant feature of a temple's outer appearance, eventually overshadowing the inner sanctuary which became obscured from view by the colossal size of the <i>gopuram</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg/250px-India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg/375px-India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg/500px-India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1639" data-file-height="1852" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:India_roadway_map_with_population_density.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing highway distribution with population density</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South India has an extensive road network with 20,573&#160;km (12,783&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_(India)" title="National Highway (India)">National Highways</a> and 46,813&#160;km (29,088&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/State_Highway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="State Highway (India)">State Highways</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Quadrilateral" title="Golden Quadrilateral">Golden Quadrilateral</a> connects Chennai in the region with Mumbai via Bangalore and Kolkata via Visakhapatnam.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Bus services are provided by state run transport corporations namely <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu_State_Transport_Corporation" title="Tamil Nadu State Transport Corporation">Tamil Nadu State Transport Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karnataka_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Karnataka State Road Transport Corporation">Karnataka State Road Transport Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Andhra Pradesh State Road Transport Corporation">Andhra Pradesh State Road Transport Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Telangana_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Telangana State Road Transport Corporation">Telangana State Road Transport Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kerala_State_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Kerala State Road Transport Corporation">Kerala State Road Transport Corporation</a><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Puducherry_Road_Transport_Corporation" title="Puducherry Road Transport Corporation">Puducherry Road Transport Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Great Southern India Railway Company was founded in England in 1853 and registered in 1859.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Construction of track in Madras Presidency began in 1859 and the 80 miles (130&#160;km) link from <a href="/wiki/Tiruchirappalli" title="Tiruchirappalli">Trichinopoly</a> to <a href="/wiki/Nagapattinam" title="Nagapattinam">Negapatam</a> was opened in 1861. The Carnatic Railway Company was founded in 1864 and opened a Madras-<a href="/wiki/Arakkonam" title="Arakkonam">Arakkonam</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kancheepuram" class="mw-redirect" title="Kancheepuram">Conjeevaram</a> - <a href="/w/index.php?title=Katpadi_junction&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Katpadi junction (page does not exist)">Katpadi junction</a>  line in 1865. The Great Southern India Railway was subsequently merged with the Carnatic Railway in 1874 to form the <a href="/wiki/South_Indian_Railway_Company" title="South Indian Railway Company">South Indian Railway Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> In 1880, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Indian_Peninsula_Railway" title="Great Indian Peninsula Railway">Great Indian Peninsula Railway</a> established by the <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British</a>, built a railway network radiating inward from <a href="/wiki/Madras" class="mw-redirect" title="Madras">Madras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> In 1879, the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Railway" title="Madras Railway">Madras Railway</a> constructed a railway line from <a href="/wiki/Royapuram" title="Royapuram">Royapuram</a> to Bangalore and the Maharaja of Mysore established <a href="/wiki/Mysore_State_Railway" title="Mysore State Railway">Mysore State Railway</a> to carryout extension from Bangalore to <a href="/wiki/Mysore" title="Mysore">Mysore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> In order to get access to West Coast and Malabar region of the country through <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Quilon" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Quilon">Port of Quilon</a>, the Maharajah <a href="/wiki/Uthram_Thirunal_Marthanda_Varma" title="Uthram Thirunal Marthanda Varma">Uthram Thirunal</a> of <a href="/wiki/Travancore" title="Travancore">Travancore</a> built <a href="/wiki/Kollam%E2%80%93Sengottai_branch_line" title="Kollam–Sengottai branch line">Quilon-Madras rail line</a> jointly with <a href="/wiki/South_Indian_Railway_Company" title="South Indian Railway Company">South Indian Railway Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Presidency" title="Madras Presidency">Madras Presidency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Madras_and_Southern_Mahratta_Railway" title="Madras and Southern Mahratta Railway">Madras and Southern Mahratta Railway</a> was founded on 1 January 1908 by merging the Madras Railway and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Mahratta_Railway" title="Southern Mahratta Railway">Southern Mahratta Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 April 1951, the Madras and Southern Mahratta Railway, the South Indian Railway and the Mysore State Railway were merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Railway (India)">Southern Railway</a>, the first zone of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Railways" title="Indian Railways">Indian Railways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Railway_zone" title="South Central Railway zone">South Central zone</a> was created on 2 October 1966 as the ninth zone of Indian Railways and the <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Railway_zone" title="South Western Railway zone">South Western zone</a> was created on 1 April 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Most of the region is covered by the three zones with small portions of coasts covered by <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Railway_zone" title="East Coast Railway zone">East Coast Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konkan_Railway" title="Konkan Railway">Konkan Railway</a>. Metro rail is operated by <a href="/wiki/Namma_Metro" title="Namma Metro">Namma Metro</a> in Bangalore, <a href="/wiki/Chennai_Metro" title="Chennai Metro">Chennai Metro</a> in Chennai, <a href="/wiki/Kochi_Metro" title="Kochi Metro">Kochi Metro</a> in Kochi and <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad_Metro" title="Hyderabad Metro">Hyderabad Metro</a> in Hyderabad. <a href="/wiki/Chennai_MRTS" class="mw-redirect" title="Chennai MRTS">Chennai MRTS</a> provides suburban rail services in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> and was the first elevated railway line in India.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nilgiri_Mountain_Railway" title="Nilgiri Mountain Railway">Nilgiri Mountain Railway</a> is a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size: 85%">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 1930, a discussion initiated by Pilot G. Vlasto led to the founding of Madras Flying Club which became a pioneer in pilot training South India.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> On 15 October 1932, Indian aviator <a href="/wiki/J._R._D._Tata" title="J. R. D. Tata">J. R. D. Tata</a> flew a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Puss_Moth" title="De Havilland Puss Moth">Puss Moth</a> aircraft carrying mail from <a href="/wiki/Karachi_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Karachi airport">Karachi</a> to <a href="/wiki/Juhu_aerodrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Juhu aerodrome">Bombay</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>) and the aircraft continued to Madras (currently Chennai) piloted by Neville Vincent, a former <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> pilot and friend of Tata.<sup id="cite_ref-history_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 9 international airports, 2 customs airports, 15 domestic airports and 11 air bases in South India. Chennai airport serves as the regional headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Airports_Authority_of_India" title="Airports Authority of India">Airports Authority of India</a> for the southern region of India comprising the states of Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka, Kerala, Tamil Nadu and Telangana and the union territories of Puducherry and Lakshadweep.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kempegowda_International_Airport" title="Kempegowda International Airport">Bengaluru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai_International_Airport" title="Chennai International Airport">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Rajiv Gandhi International Airport">Hyderabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochin_International_Airport" title="Cochin International Airport">Kochi</a> are amongst the 10 busiest airports in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Air_Command,_Indian_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Air Command, Indian Air Force">Southern Air Command</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> is headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Thiruvananthapuram" title="Thiruvananthapuram">Thiruvananthapuram</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Training_Command,_Indian_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Training Command, Indian Air Force">Training Command</a> is headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bengaluru.</a> The Indian Air Force operates eleven air bases in Southern India including two in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a> operates airbases at <a href="/wiki/INS_Garuda" title="INS Garuda">Kochi</a>, <a href="/wiki/INS_Rajali" title="INS Rajali">Arakkonam</a>, <a href="/wiki/INS_Parundu" title="INS Parundu">Uchipuli</a>, <a href="/wiki/INS_Dega" title="INS Dega">Vizag</a>, <a href="/wiki/INS_Baaz" title="INS Baaz">Campbell Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/INS_Kohassa" title="INS Kohassa">Diglipur</a> in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_India&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A total of 89 ports are situated along the coast: Tamil Nadu (15), Karnataka (10), Kerala (17), Andhra Pradesh (12), Lakshadweep (10), Pondicherry (2) and Andaman &amp; Nicobar (23).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Major ports include <a href="/wiki/Chennai_Port" title="Chennai Port">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visakhapatnam_Port" title="Visakhapatnam Port">Visakhapatnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mangalore_Port" title="New Mangalore Port">Mangalore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuticorin_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuticorin Port">Tuticorin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ennore_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Ennore Port">Ennore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochin_Port_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Cochin Port Trust">Kochi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Kollam,_Mar_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg/220px-Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg/330px-Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg/440px-Port_of_Kollam%2C_Mar_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Kollam,_Mar_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kollam_Port" title="Kollam Port">Port of Quilon (Kollam)</a></div></div></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kerala_backwaters" title="Kerala backwaters">Kerala backwaters</a> are a network of interconnected canals, rivers, lakes and inlets, a labyrinthine system formed by more than 900&#160;km of waterways. In the midst of this landscape, there are a number of towns and cities, which serve as the starting and end points of transportation services and backwater cruises.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Naval_Command" title="Eastern Naval Command">Eastern Naval Command</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Naval_Command" title="Southern Naval Command">Southern Naval Command</a> of the Indian Navy are headquartered at Visakhapatnam and Kochi, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> The Indian Navy has its major operational bases in Visakhapatnam, Chennai, Kochi, Karwar and Kavaratti in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
